#Recaps - EOS
For now the "#Recaps - EOS" aim just to provide weekly leads to some posts in the Telegram EOS group (https://t.me/EOSproject) deemed to potentially be of interest for many in the EOS community.

#Open_Source: https://words.filippo.io/professional-maintainers/
"Open Source software runs the Internet, and by extension the economy. This is an undisputed fact about reality in 2021. And yet, the role of Open Source maintainer has failed to mature from a hobby into a proper profession."

#EOS: https://t.me/EOSproject/1908240
"EOS has the opportunity to brand itself as 'The Home for Open Source Software'. Large open source communities should be head-hunted and their migration to EOS sponsored. You could think of ways to tokenize maintenance. The chain is entertaining the thought of sponsoring Fractally. It could similarly think about sponsoring other/all OS projects."

#Market_Cap : https://t.me/EOSproject/1911275
Q - "Is there any official rule/policy/strategy/consensus around EOS Market cap?"
A - "That this is a project doing a lot of building of actual software and structures of cooperation and decentralization. It is not vapor ware, or promises to build that bring on speculation and expectation of price. Therefore:
1) it requires time for all of these things to be completed
2) It will require adequate advertising and informing of the public of what had been built.
3) It will require that the market is not a bear market where everything is crashing, and there is no interest in investing."

#Meeting_purpose : https://t.me/EdenOSinfo/41448 :
--CD1-- : ‚ÄúMeetings are supposed to be held to achieve something, not to waste everyone time and tap each other on the back on how many meetings we had. Deliveries are the metrics, not meetings- those are time sink on itself. Same is true for eden and especially fractally (since it has more meetings)‚Äù
--M1-- : ‚ÄúThe aim is to get more people to join and have them contribute to the community that should be the goal...that's what is lacking on eos and eden itself.‚Äù
--M2-- : ‚ÄúThe first question is, what are those people who are members, doing to produce value?‚Äù
--M3-- : ‚ÄúIf people are not aligned they can't build meaningful consensus and that will stop progress.‚Äù ‚Äì ‚Äú‚ÄùI think each CD should have clear goals, let their intention be known and consensus reached to prevent back and forth.‚Äù‚Äù
--M1-- : ‚ÄúA good way to grow a community is to find good incentivization mechanisms for new members who are joining....The heart and soul of the fractals is to get people to be aligned for whatever cause they're trying to achieve...in this case they're finding ways on how to contribute to Eden or EOS.‚Äù
--M2-- : ‚ÄúI think we agree on most of what you've said. Although, to me, and I assume many non-participants in the EdenFractal, the exact contributions they've made are not well known.‚Äù
--M4-- : ‚ÄúAn individual's contribution and influence over the network is much more discernable via fractally as more of EOS becomes aware of the new potential, old and new approaches to problems solving will adjust accordingly.‚Äù
--M5-- : ‚ÄúIt's time for everyone to come to terms with the fact that Eden's progress has been stifled (or at least limited) when Eden resources are used on Fractally. I include delegates' time as a resource here, or at least I did for myself when I was one.‚Äù
--CD1-- : ‚ÄúMy words are strong on this topic because i want to force the issue in eden community- i fully realize i am probably making more enemies that way- but at the same time i am not willing to spend time in community that cherishes meetings more than code.‚Äù
--CD2-- : ‚ÄúI think its a neat experiment, and I like the individuals involved, but I think there are some hard questions that need to be answered in terms of how the fractally concept will actually add value to a community.‚Äù
--CD3-- : ‚ÄúSomething that we can learn from our experiences so far is how we treat each other in the community. I will vote for people who respect their fellow community members and encourage everyone else to do so as well.‚Äù

#ESPx - Eden Smart Proxy : https://t.me/EdenOSinfo/46309 : "ESPx aims to ... " - https://proxy.eden.eoscommunity.org/
- --M1-- : "... as far as i can tell, people voting for proxy dont get a say who is in it ..."
- --M2-- : "They have a say. 3 ways.
1) They can undelegate if they don't support the proxy.
2) They can participate in Eden election to have a more direct say.
3) If they don't want to participate in the election, they can talk to those eden members who have a say in how the proxy will cast the votes. (Currently the broker who de-facto controling the BP is largely unknown in the community, no way for community to influence him to decide whom to sell the votes)"
--exM-- : "One major issue is the naming of things. That term Eden seems to be confusing a lot of people. Naming things are very important. Eden, EdenOS, EdenonEos, Eden fractally. What do you know about each one and its relationships?"
--CD-A-- : https://t.me/EdenOSinfo/46617 : "https://www.edenelections.com/post/eden-governance-gets-a-rocket-up-its-community"

#EOS_BP Rotation : https://t.me/EOSproject/1969982 : "BP rotation over the last 1 year. 28 different BPs have produced at least one block" - "On EOS, each of the top 21 nodes rotate constantly. Even if one of them decide to not include certain types of tx in a block, it'd only be another .5 seconds until next BP would potentially add it to next block. All 21 BPs would need to censor for a tx to not be able to make it on-chain"

#EOS_BP - few of the flood of posts : https://t.me/EOSproject/1969995 :
--M1-- : "What is ESPx trying to solve for? The regulated exchanges?""
--M2-- : "1) The primary thing it's trying to solve is multiple producers (real or fake) owned by one entity. In the early days, proof of ...
2) The other thing it's trying to solve is separate direct involvement with governance from exchanges.
3) And the third thing is ... "
--M3-- : "People criticize EOS by pointing out how ETH2 or other POS chains have thousands of validators compared to 21 producing BPs because it is really just a small handful of entities running a ton of nodes because that's how their consensus works in POS."
--M2-- : "https://t.me/EOSproject/1970014 - "Provide exchanges an alternative source of yield on their balance that does not involve governance and they wouldn't even need to run a block producer, let alone be directly involved with governance.""
